# Cheap Ass 6x2 Pneumatic Belt Setup. 3D printed Pulley/ Vex Versa Pulley. Thingiverse link in post #534

### Replies: 960 Views: 19896

## \#1 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-08-21T05:40:07.758Z Reads: 1068

```
Decided to document this setup in its own thread to showcasing the performance and invite discussions. It was also brought to my attention that I was spamming the no words thread. I agree, it would be best to wait until the project is done and reserve the incremental updates to this thread. 

What is needed(3D printed Pulley + 3D printed pulley adapter)
1. Tire with hub from aliexpress. 
$69 for a set of 4 (shipping included)
https://www.aliexpress.com/item/free-shipping-6X2-tyre-6-Inch-Scooter-Tire-Inner-Tube-Set-Electric-Scooter-Wheel-Chair/32840489792.html 
2. Three M6 Bolt, 45mm length
$7 for 25pcs
https://www.mcmaster.com/#91292a143/=1e8wvz4 
3. 3D printed  pulley adapter 
https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/14AF8h_PFzBTdH6JRkKynJ70I3WzezC0N
4. 3D printed pulley(Any teeth count from 42 to 60)
https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/14AF8h_PFzBTdH6JRkKynJ70I3WzezC0N
5. Trucks
$65
should have 8mm shaft with 35mm free length. TB218 will work.
products/torqueboards-218mm-trucks 


What is needed(Vex Robotics Pulley + 3D printed pulley adapter)
2. Three M6 Bolt, 25mm length
3. 3D printed Versa pulley adapter
https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/14AF8h_PFzBTdH6JRkKynJ70I3WzezC0N
4. Vex robotics versa pulley(42T or 60T, 18mm)
$5.99
https://www.vexrobotics.com/vexpro/motion/belts-and-pulleys/htdversapulley.html
6. three qty of locknut(8-32)
$6 for pack of 50
https://www.mcmaster.com/90101a009
7. 3 qty of bolt(8-32) 1-1/4" . you'll have to grind it a tiny bit
$6 for 50 pcs
https://www.mcmaster.com/92196a201

Pics:
![MVIMG_20180818_223405|666x500](upload://7SJUloXyjcOYJiRACBtT7qni3vl.jpg)
![MVIMG_20180818_233203|666x500](upload://2wszSJPmKYeFUVaQHa3HNVRqK5a.jpg)
![fb85e18431863a4b842d622e24e7bf74900ff36d_1_443x500|443x500](upload://yG8YQmkMpn8OBrrvkqNcjzM445M.jpg)
![d6144d2a08db3348291e757f3f79d255f965d984_1_483x500|483x500](upload://nYskJJdKNFksnTDLPiIardSy88X.jpg)
![MVIMG_20180821_004435|666x500](upload://eJJ6gfftn0z23wGBbHCT2FpIUoH.jpg)
![MVIMG_20180821_004516|666x500](upload://qA2cHgbVTdn4dx8KBZ4ddxGpEyk.jpg)
Tire above has been pressurized to 60psi. 

Now I wait for 2 weeks to receive the other 3 wheels so that I can test it on a board. 
I don't have long axle trucks to properly test the wobble, but I did spin it on a normal truck and didn't notice any wobbling. Can't say anything about balance. How do you guys test for that?

Any comments?

EDIT1:
Modified the part to save plastic
![image|493x500](upload://TJbWTt1CTX6LKIe0miemL6CTDu.jpeg) 
![3Dprinted_pulley_assembly|437x500](upload://zfwsKpbcOTSAQEN1Zti2Rx8sR8h.jpeg)

![MVIMG_20180921_180021|516x500](upload://pUxILJ5lEcpwCLZ9sjPSPRzH6Fd.jpeg)
```

## \#2 Posted by: Maxid Posted at: 2018-08-21T06:07:18.869Z Reads: 870

```
you can eliminate wobble by using some tire pearls - I did that to mine and had no issues with wobble afterwards even on 3D printed hubs.
```

## \#4 Posted by: TheImmortalJew Posted at: 2018-08-22T00:59:06.181Z Reads: 868

```
My experience has been mostly positive with these hubs and tires. I took a slightly different approach to the wheel pulley. I utilized the 3 hub bolts to attach a 3D printed adapter that fits the profile of VEX Robotics versa pulleys. The pulley presses onto the spokes of the adapter and then (3) 8-32 bolts hold the pulley in place. 

I'm running enertion motor mounts with 15T motor pulley and 345-5M-15 belts. The wheels run quite true, I've had them up to 35 mph no problem on 12s5p/FOCBOX. 

And yes you need TB 218 trucks.

![20180821_204102|690x335](upload://8q34kJBmSrgdGiuCa7fFPvo0nZL.jpg)

![20180821_204220|690x335](upload://vSXCGHIvBfTpDXAsq0W6rh7NuhQ.jpg)
```

```
I'm currently testing something similar (inexpensive tire option with 3D printed hubs). Below I've posted my current 3D model as well as the tires I'm planning to use. Parts have been 3D printed, I have the tire from amazon, and the bolts to screw them together come in Thursday.

Main reason I'm testing these tires is they're super inexpensive (they were on sale for $5 each at the time I purchased them). They are from amazon which means they are super accessible and quick to receive, and they're semi pneumatic (no airing them up) which is technically less maintenance at the expense of customization. 

I'll post the 3D models over here as well at the end of the week assuming they work well after I've tested them.
```

## \#7 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-08-22T05:54:00.775Z Reads: 751

```
Design looks nice, but I don't think these tires are mean for anything serious. From amazon: "These tires are ideal for hand trucks, lawnmowers, utility carts, and other lawn and garden equipment". So basically not meant for speed. But be safe when testing them.

The 6x2 tires are however proven to be reliable around here. You could get them from 
https://psychotiller.com
or if you don't mind waiting for 2-3 weeks from here:
https://www.aliexpress.com/item/free-shipping-6X2-tyre-6-Inch-Scooter-Tire-Inner-Tube-Set-Electric-Scooter-Wheel-Chair-Truck/32840489792.html
Apparently there is a discount of 15% in 6 days.
```

## \#11 Posted by: Alphamail Posted at: 2018-08-22T16:16:59.350Z Reads: 694

```
Straight cut gears will be noisier but you won't have the axial load you will get with helical

[https://khkgears.net/new/gear_knowledge/gear_technical_reference/gear_forces.html](https://khkgears.net/new/gear_knowledge/gear_technical_reference/gear_forces.html)

[https://www.youtube.com/watch?reload=9&v=PANVccyJuFI](https://www.youtube.com/watch?reload=9&v=PANVccyJuFI)
```

---
## \#12 Posted by: Maxid Posted at: 2018-08-22T17:25:29.268Z Reads: 673

```
Sure but who cares about axial load when you have a factory made grub screw hole in the motor shaft? As I said this is for 5065 motors that also have the added benefit of having a cut shaft (=perfect for experimenting with 3D printed gears) plus grub screw. You can even buy them with a thread on the motor shaft - axial loads should thus not be an issue.
```

```
A bit confused. Where is the grub screw located? The axial load will get transferred to the bearing which are built to work mostly with radial load. I think that's what he's talking about. Am I missing something?

You can probably go with double helical gear which 3D printing won't care about. As for the drive double helical gear, one can even get it printed in metal(SS) if machined part is expensive.
https://www.shapeways.com/materials.steel
```

## \#21 Posted by: MoeStooge Posted at: 2018-08-22T22:34:49.074Z Reads: 598

```
Helicals need perfect alignment.  Axiel load = wasted power and should have a thrust bearing.  Precision square cut in oil are stronger, more efficient, more forgiving, and quiet enough. Good luck with Helicals.
```

## \#24 Posted by: Maxid Posted at: 2018-08-23T08:20:33.679Z Reads: 584

```
with double helical you lose the advantage of always having two teeth in contact simultaneously because at a reasonable gear angle you don't reach the required teeth length as the total gear length is limited.
```

```
Figured I would give a small update on the one's I'm working on since I have a similar goal to you (cheap effective pneumatics). ## \#39 Posted by: DragonSwagin Posted at: 2018-08-27T21:52:00.969Z Reads: 544
```

```
I'll post the STL files and solidworks models once I've tested the design and made sure it's 100% safe (should be finished up by the end of this week). Until then, I'll post a picture of the solidworks assembly, and a close up of the wheels. It uses 6x M6 55mm bolts for the wheel+pulley, and 40mm bolts for just the wheel. These wheels fit on standard caliber 2 trucks.

https://i.gyazo.com/4dfac57355259f1a06b5043b71f75821.png

These pictures I'm posting only have the 3 bolts in the wheel (I was just sizing at the time). The ones I actually have on my board right now use all 6 bolts. Bearings were pressed into place using the butt of a metal utility flashlight. One crucial thing about this design is that you don't overtighten the bolts as it will crush the plastic and cause the wheel to wobble due to unbalance. If 100% effort was brute strength tightening, you only use about 5-10% effort to tighten the nut/bolt against the plastic.

![IMG_0815%20(3)|375x500](upload://kddW9TOJPxkdNIxII3Jbdt1pKFS.jpg)![IMG_0813%20(3)|666x500](upload://fzLAPPGS0zxvUUipDASTGtWtkEH.jpg)![IMG_0814%20(3)|666x500](upload://jrGm9ZCLJwkaeR6nZgK9MZbtsXN.jpg)
```

## \#41 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-08-27T23:28:59.231Z Reads: 503

```
May I suggest putting big washers for each bolt and nut,  or just use flanged bolts and nuts. that will give you good compression force without destroying the plastic. 

The way I dealt with it is: I set the electric drill to a certain torque and tried it on a piece to make sure it doesn't damage the plastic. Once that torque setting it known, you can reliably use that every single time.

BTW, what is the approximate cost of 3D printing in cu inch for you?
```

---
## \#42 Posted by: DragonSwagin Posted at: 2018-08-28T01:01:56.990Z Reads: 513

```
Washers would be a great idea, I just didn't order any with the bolts as I eventually got a feel for how tight to screw the bolts. 

My roommate has a fairly nice 3D printer, so he'll pump out prints so long as I have filament. I used PETG filament and it's $25/kg for a quality roll. Comes out to ~787cc of volume, but that's usually higher since I used a 50% infill. 

4 full wheels and a pulley probably take a little under a kilogram of plastic, however I'm unsure since I went through 2 rolls printing prototypes and the final wheels for this project of mine :sweat_smile:
```

## \#47 Posted by: JasperM Posted at: 2018-08-29T11:32:55.206Z Reads: 484

```
Hey mate are the dimensions of the hubs and pulley set correct as per the real life product, I've notices the slot for the bearings measures 24mm not 22mm like skate bearings.

Do the designs need to be scaled?

Other then that the system looks good, I may have to try and see if they will fit with dual SK3s.
```

---
## \#48 Posted by: DragonSwagin Posted at: 2018-08-29T18:04:39.279Z Reads: 492

```
Depending on what you're 3D printing and the material used and how accurate your printer is, you have to make the hole slightly larger than 22mm as you don't get that perfect precision you can get with a CNC machining out aluminum. I'm not sure if 24mm is too much in this case, however for my design I ended up making it a 23mm hole for the bearing so that you could press fit them in and they would be tight. The first one I made where the dimension was 22mm I ended up crushing the plastic trying to press fit the bearing in.

However these are not my files, so I'm unsure of why he went with 24mm.
```

## \#58 Posted by: DragonSwagin Posted at: 2018-08-30T22:17:56.940Z Reads: 479

```
Alright after doing a little riding, I'm running into a significant issue with the pneumatics I'm testing, battery life. On the original hard wheels I have, I could go ~18 miles on full battery. With the pneumatics I'm testing right now, this range has decreased to about 3.5 miles. There are three main issues I think this stems from.
1. I'm using pneumatics. I already know there's increased rolling friction and was expecting to lose about half my battery life, but not 80% of it.
2. The pneumatics have a really aggressive tread and they're very flat at the contact point (all 1.5 inches of the tire is on the ground). 
3. Poor design in my hubs. It could very well be that my wheel hub designs are having an unforseen impact on this that I haven't figured out. 

For my commute, I need my board to safely go 6 miles (which is why I was hoping it would stay in the 8 or 9 mile range). I'm trying to figure out if I should drop the money on a bigger battery, scrap the pnuematics I was working on and go with one of the other designs above for scooter tires, or some other unseen option I haven't thought of yet.

Thoughts?

-Also, it may be worth noting that if I spin the wheels with my hand, they roll forever (good bearings working like they should). However, when I push myself on the board and roll to a stop, I stop after only about 5 feet of free rolling since there's so much friction.
```

---
## \#59 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-08-30T22:23:53.145Z Reads: 460

```
So basically the quality of rubber+tire is unsuitable for speed. Well, you tried. Time to get those cheap true pneumatic wheels :D
```

---
## \#66 Posted by: ervinelin Posted at: 2018-09-09T00:26:43.320Z Reads: 444

```
So I have these as well and the free rolling is terrible. So I opened up the hub, hammered out the existing bearings which I think were not good to begin with (some Rusty and grind when turned). Then I used a carbide grinding bit to thin the inner bearing seat so that the new bearings I bought would be pressfit instead of hammer fit.

This made the wheel turn much much much better...

Also, all but 1 were off balanced, I used 5g weights to balance them as best as I could to prevent wobbles when rotating. Usually this is placed on the opposite end of the tube inlet.
```

## \#88 Posted by: amazingdave Posted at: 2018-09-10T15:25:31.082Z Reads: 438

```
Made a balancer out of some little brushless motors with no magnets... 

The wheels are very well balanced. No lathe work required...

The tyres are a different story though! Got them all balanced with stick on weights eventually. 

![image|375x500](upload://woqOIHuw5COXDp9tibqP99ofBrc.jpeg)![image|375x500](upload://1Nlk0D9Nhjjkiks6HIJXqt3CS0L.jpeg)![image|375x500](upload://dorazvj9mbTqqgmUxAOKEa9JfZT.jpeg)
```

---
## \#89 Posted by: Okami Posted at: 2018-09-10T18:58:03.403Z Reads: 413

```
Mind to share a few more details? Did u just spin the wheel and checked where it wobbles?

Also about 'sticks'. Did u just glue wood pieces on tire to make it stable?

@amazingdave
```

---
## \#90 Posted by: amazingdave Posted at: 2018-09-10T19:09:43.303Z Reads: 424

```
@Okami
 I used the mini brushless motors as low friction bearings so that the heavy part of the wheel drops to the bottom under its own weight. Skate bearings are not good enough.... I then used these automotive adhesive wheel balancing weights from Amazon (stick on!) opposite the heavy point until the wheel does not have a bias one way or the other. Then I tested by spinning them quickly to check that my balancing was correct. 

![image|230x500](upload://oXx7IcuVXpS4NuZuKDvRcZrTtib.jpeg)
```

```
It is a bummer tires themselves are not balanced at times..
```

## \#153 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-09-23T21:54:42.804Z Reads: 350

```
Since people don't want to 3D print the pulley or don't have access to a 3D printer. I made an adapter to use with vex robotics versa pulley. It's a much smaller part to print and won't take a lot of money. I have ordered a couple of vex robotics 60T pulley to show you guys how it fits. I can send them to whoever's interested. Pay me shipping + what I paid for.

Files at https://drive.google.com/open?id=14AF8h_PFzBTdH6JRkKynJ70I3WzezC0N
```

## \#214 Posted by: Bataleon Posted at: 2018-11-09T19:47:18.685Z Reads: 264

```
+1 The wheels linked above take 628Z (8mm x 24mm x 8mm) bearings instead of regular 608 (8mm x 22mm x 7mm) longboard bearings. So the axle diameter is the same, but other dimensions are different.
```

## \#238 Posted by: kalebludlow Posted at: 2018-11-24T22:22:42.292Z Reads: 248

```
Hey @mishrasubhransu I'm using the 50T non-spoke 3D printed pulley, and the bolts I got thread through the plastic and therefore won't let me fully tighten the rim, any chance I could get a modified file with a slightly bigger hole to avoid threading?
```

---
## \#239 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-11-25T01:44:13.210Z Reads: 253

```
3D printing can reduce the hole diameter a bit, so I would suggest to put the screw in through the hole while keeping the power tool rotating anticlockwise. That basically makes the diameter just perfect.

Else if you have a a 6mm drill bit, that will work too. 

Do I make sense?

BTW, got any pics of the setup?
```

---
## \#240 Posted by: kalebludlow Posted at: 2018-11-25T02:03:53.283Z Reads: 249

```
I'll see what drill bits I have, when I get home I'll send a photo
```

```
1 pair x @accrobrandon
1 pair x @Bataleon
1 pair x @deucesdown

2 pair x @Lambjr088

1 last pair remains, if you let me know before 3pm tomorrow, I can send it in the same trip to USPS.
```

## \#286 Posted by: Benjamin899 Posted at: 2018-12-08T01:47:16.728Z Reads: 222

```
looks nice, are you going to make it metal?
```

---
## \#287 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-12-08T03:27:23.629Z Reads: 221

```
Probably not. Had this design rotting in a folder for a while, so just gave it a print. Basically this attaches to a **disc brake plate**.  The placement of holes on the disc meant I had to have the same holes on the wheel and that was less than idea because they are **closer to center**. So I made these **locking features** to hold the rim in place. They will probably fail and then I'll think of a proper design for disc brakes.  Haha.
```

---
## \#288 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-12-08T05:12:03.854Z Reads: 230

```
If anyone has access to cnc or wants to have it made in aluminum, I can give you the files for free.  BTW, these are meant to go on the front wheels. 

If you are thinking of CNCing then there is also a cheaper way than making the entire wheel. It will basically be an adapter that attaches to the aliexpress wheels. I'll post it here in a few days. 


![IMG_20181208_000142|666x500](upload://qAulfHj2cALdntbwIpuswLbb4rH.jpeg) ![IMG_20181208_000203|666x500](upload://nVPfaj6gEj3d03Cjn5AsUjbxoZ5.jpeg) ![IMG_20181208_000443|666x500](upload://vDC3AoOl9srRrQlJA9paRWgnkZI.jpeg)
```

## \#329 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-13T17:15:08.568Z Reads: 212

```
Printing PETG at 255'C is quite sturdy by itself and PETG is cheap, but fiddly to print. I don't know how strong nylon is yet, but PETG at 255'C is way stronger than ABS I used for pulleys before. Hell, I even used a 15T motor pulley printed from PETG for 300KM until it just melted. My motor was a 5045, way too small(I am 100 kilos) and usually reached 90'C+. :slight_smile:
```

## \#336 Posted by: skatardude10 Posted at: 2018-12-13T18:50:35.875Z Reads: 212

```
Thanks @accrobrandon.

Yep, here you go  @Trdolan03, these are @ptowncruiser's hubs that I've modified for a slightly better fit, more strength in the rim portions, and added additional third bearing for the pulley portion of the hubs. I don't think these with the third bearing will fit on standard calibers, but if you have TB218s or caliber-Es they should work fine with the third bearing. They might even fit without the third bearing, I'd measure it up in CAD first and use some calipers on your trucks to check though. If not, I'd recommend following the link to @ptowncruiser's original cad for these hubs in the thingiverse link thing description below. If you want you can even use his pulley and main hub with my outer thickened rim portion for more strength, they should be 100% compatible with each other.

https://www.thingiverse.com/thing:3056762
```

## \#348 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-13T20:32:57.769Z Reads: 210

```
If it still has the tube that feeds the plastic (bowden system) I wouldn't go to such adventures as printing in PETG..

![46|690x388](upload://rIDi5VBbYfLzIcOTek22SsVsi3n.jpeg) 

Stringing is a mess to remove and also you can't really print at 250-255'C to not melt the teflon tube inside your heater.

Of course still having a bowden+full metal (saves your teflon tube from heat) I managed to print some nice gears:

![08|690x388](upload://cd8WWmX7vfx5uM8PVbzWJ5AC4kw.jpeg) 

By then I just upgraded my printer to direct feed and never seen strings of plastic again.
```

## \#350 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-13T21:39:55.716Z Reads: 193

```
I mean.. You should be able to take half of the rim off as is.. It's the nylocks outside the rim. You remove the hanger bolt, remove the 3 nylock nuts and take one part of the hub off. Pulley, second part of the hub, etc. stays on. Change it and ride on after doing everything in reverse.
```

## \#365 Posted by: banjaxxed Posted at: 2018-12-18T00:16:13.823Z Reads: 192

## \#366 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-18T08:12:38.326Z Reads: 203

```
I mean, you could. But I wouldn't trust my life on PETG being printed at 240'C. If it's winter and room is colder, layer adhesion will be below tolerable, hell, even layer splitting can appear.

I am talking about real PETG, not PET. That stuff(PETG) is recommended to print at 250'C+. I got best results at 255'C, but it also depends on your hotend, thermistor, nozzle, speed, either you use a silicone sock for the heater block, active cooling is through the roof, etc.

Source: been printing prototypes for companies for well over a few years now.

Example prints done using converted anycubic with PETG at 255'C:
![21|690x388](upload://5NpIMXilybhHaHK4VuoFFfVkfZQ.jpeg) 
![15|281x500](upload://7UbfZfqYmlJDGAj047AVEFPqBGB.jpeg) ![52|690x388](upload://mKS5lTnxf4PO2PWuK1B4bTUPvqU.jpeg) 
(Don't mind the pet hair, I am a Disney princess xD)

Stringing? Nah.
```

---
## \#374 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-18T09:20:23.388Z Reads: 190

```
I would go for the full metal hotend or even titan aero extruder system if you have the bucks and are not afraid to get your hands/mind dirty with custom firmware. Also grabbing a BLTouch would help immensely(who doesn't love automatic bed leveling?). Also means more firmware. All parts can be purchased as either clones(the titan aero, 3DTouch) or legit(ender3 full metal hotend) from AliExpress or related stores.

I will ask my colleague which full metal hotend he got later.

I'd still rather go for a direct approach as full metal has another issue, it might clog like hell during retractions. With bowden you have your tube inserted almost to the opening of the nozzle, this allows you to do ridiculous retractions like 5-10mm without problems. This also means if you go above the melting/charring point of the tube, you will get some nasty particles around..

With full metal it(the bowden tube) ends at the "throat"(the heatbreak) that connects the hot part with your nozzle to the heatsink, keeping the incoming plastic sturdy enough, to be melted later. This introduces a small gap between the tube and the metal, which might end up with swelling of the filament and eventual jam when doing retractions >2mm.

Clarification: direct uses full metal, but not that much retraction, like up to 1mm

I mean this could be useful information for everyone, but I don't know. If it doesn't hurt anyones eyes, I will continue to help/explain here. :slight_smile:
```

---
## \#375 Posted by: banjaxxed Posted at: 2018-12-18T09:27:12.817Z Reads: 178

```
I have printed in PETG yes PETG many times successfully at 238-242 without an all metal hotend on multiple printers. The filament is all important, the room temp not so much as it doesn‚Äôt warp like ABS, ABS+ is a little better in that regard
```

---
## \#376 Posted by: banjaxxed Posted at: 2018-12-18T09:31:21.266Z Reads: 182

```
Charing occurs above 244c but yes any inaccuracies of the thermistor and it will start to degrade, I use cornacopia knock-off from AliExpress with good results & it‚Äôs cheap 

Best to stay out of the room and vent it afterwards if worried
```

---
## \#377 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-18T09:31:52.890Z Reads: 200

```
I did not say you couldn't. I am also saying it's superior to ABS. Have you tested the layer adhesion with a tension, torsion, impact testing equipment? You'd be surprised what kind of performance PETG gains at those temperatures.

Hell, I've been riding PRINTED wheels for 300+ kilometers. 20% infill, PETG.

![42|690x388](upload://so2kYiRLQ4HehA6C1qTevkn6HoZ.jpeg) ![21|690x388](upload://gEDnlmKDacnfF1BJRFZuy1pnBpi.jpeg) ![30|690x388](upload://lnHe1t2aL43cmCw7mw3Ig8f3wlw.jpeg) ![09|690x388](upload://hY3bzG5u4Iruus3ETVQhvVKf3sS.jpg) 

I am just talking from experience. 255'C prints is minimum strength I can accept by now.

Oh yeah, the motor mount is printed too.. From PETG. :smiley:

And this is how it looked like after I replaced the mount and the motor(5045 with 100 kilos is a no-no). Wheels still printed and heavily used:

![04|690x388](upload://kdQqB2OZdK9JnclRV2Oou2gzVkV.jpeg)
```

## \#379 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-18T09:44:36.416Z Reads: 199

```
I am using the cheapest, but for sure "pure" PETG from Poland "DevilDesign" for 10‚Ç¨/kilo. People say it's complete garbage. I say that people who say that are complete garbage and can't dial their settings. :smiley:  (this is a joke, pls no offenses)

This is how a 6mm by 50mm pillar should look after breaking:

![impact|690x388](upload://9y08Yiu2IYe7HGLl94tnKALUqWE.jpeg) 

If it breaks at layer lines or you see perimeter/infill spacing inside, it's not bonded properly.

![image|505x307](upload://b9bxqaISj95EAiyy3fxWvRQwOhK.jpeg) 

THIS is what you want. Complete adhesion. Solid.

This is how ABS cylinder should look like for giggles:

![29|666x500](upload://sivezcDQK3batDOVXtTaXnibD77.jpeg) 

B E N D Y B O Y E
```

## \#380 Posted by: Benjamin899 Posted at: 2018-12-18T10:15:49.720Z Reads: 189

```
Could you Print wheels from Pla If settings are richtig?
```

---
## \#381 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-18T10:17:02.778Z Reads: 189

```
No, you shouldn't. Imagine the friction and centripetal forces you will get. It will MELT your rims faster than you can jump off your board at the "oh FUCK!" moment.

Glass transition(softening) temperature of PLA is ~60'C, PETG ~90'C depending on purity and additions, ABS ~105'C, etc.

My wheels used PETG for the rims and TPU(Thermo Plastic Urethane) for the tires.
```

---
## \#382 Posted by: banjaxxed Posted at: 2018-12-18T10:23:09.440Z Reads: 182

```
[quote="murloc992, post:377, topic:65559"]
Have you tested the layer adhesion with a tension, torsion, impact testing equipment?
[/quote] No I do not have access to that type of equipment, just real world testing and my results are the same with pullies but with lower printing temps 242c and 25% iirc
```

---
## \#383 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-18T10:27:35.870Z Reads: 194

```
I am glad it is, pulleys get surface load though, so there's not much trouble the teeth will wear out fast or break.

I am just stating the best strength you can get if you really want the most of your filament. 242'C in a cold environment would make my skin go full on goosebumps if I had to use it in a loaded/critical situation, it just doesn't adhere much..

For comparison, I could break the 6mm cylinder printed at 240'C with my hands before.

Later at 248'C I had to use pliers, then at 255'C equipment with a vice grip, because I couldn't make it bend much even using two pairs of pliers and my table as support edge.

It's all up to the needs of an individual.
```

---
## \#397 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-18T15:47:27.914Z Reads: 190

```
If you have a genuine prusa with a brass nozzle, [calibrated extruder](https://mattshub.com/2017/04/19/extruder-calibration/) (using PLA, lower push force, better flow), I would recommend starting at:

First Layer Bed: 90'C
First Layer Temp: 250'C
Further Bed: 90'C
Further Layers: 255'C - play around with this, depends on ambient temps and if you have [silicone sock](https://e3d-online.com/v6-socks-pro-pack-of-3), if you don't, keep at the higher side.

Fan at automatic 30-50% if MK2S/MK2.5(12V fan), constant 50% if MK3(5V fan).

If you have a [steel nozzle](https://e3d-online.com/hardened-steel-nozzles-v6) and have no [silicone sock](https://e3d-online.com/v6-socks-pro-pack-of-3), you might need to increase the temperature from 250'C up to 5 degrees, so you could even reach 260'C. With sock keep it at 255'C as it will not radiate much heat.

Your retractions might need to go to 1mm. Leave Lift-Z as is.

I have tried printing upwards to 275'C but it gave me diminishing returns around 265'C using a steel nozzle with a sock. Small details became overcooked.
```

---

---
## \#437 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-12-27T23:49:32.547Z Reads: 164

```
I can confirm that the resistance is due to the thick grease they use. They give you more resistance but require less attention. If you want less resistance then put some wd40 in there and let is dissolve the thick grease.

I made a spool mount for 3D printer using 608 bearings and they didn't let the spool holder rotate freely. So I soaked them in wd40 for 30mins and bam they became totally free.
```

---
## \#438 Posted by: deucesdown Posted at: 2018-12-28T00:38:34.294Z Reads: 171

```
WD40 is mostly kerosene and light oil. Has a teeerible reputation as a lubricant on things like bearings :) Usually you'd need to flush it out with alcohol then apply the lube of your choice.

What I'm trying to say is if you WD40, make sure you add some lube, maybe more than once.
```

---
## \#439 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-12-28T00:46:02.609Z Reads: 179

```
of course. I only used it on the 3d printer spool is because it's not going to see much speed or load. 

For the skateboard I let it be because, I don't think in larger scheme of things, there are not a significant source of loss. Hummie also uses a very thick grease in his hub motors for increasing longevity of the bearings. 

If someone changes the bearing, it would be nice for them to report back if they have significantly increased range.
```

---
## \#440 Posted by: ervinelin Posted at: 2018-12-28T00:57:22.750Z Reads: 193

```
I swapped out the bearings after hammering the original ones out (already slightly rusty), grinding down the beating seat a little and popping in new bearings.

![IMG20180906170702|281x500](upload://lBtsDuuB2TXmh4wRf8Or0Np8lIw.jpeg) 
I used a nut and bolt to hammer it out from the inside of the hub. A few good wacks was all it took.

I should have used a lathe but didn't have one on hand.

Wheels turned with a lot less resistance but I doubt I got much more range with it as the Tyre still have a high rolling resistance.

Also, popping in a new bearing without grinding down the seat was near impossible. I managed to hammer one in but it basically seized and wouldn't turn.
```

## \#455 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-28T17:20:15.304Z Reads: 168

```
Another culprit I found during this evening of playing around: the spacer is shit. It's too long. The bearings centers get pushed out once you tighten the wheel. Still unsure how much to take off, but maybe somebody with better tools could check this too.
```

---
## \#456 Posted by: Benjamin899 Posted at: 2018-12-28T18:32:32.006Z Reads: 164

```
ah damn, this makes sense. They rolled better in my hand.
```

---
## \#457 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2018-12-28T18:58:32.129Z Reads: 170

```
That maybe by design, given that the other side of the centers would be pressed when you mount them on the axle and tighten them? That way it remains centers during operation. Otherwise, they would get pushed inward into the wheel. Make sense?

If I were to design a wheel, I would do it that way.
```

---
## \#458 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-28T19:04:36.034Z Reads: 171

```
The issue is, both bearings are pressed inside the rim unevenly. Especially apparent when you tighten the wheel together and on the axle. The spacer shouldn't be so long, that one bearing is offset by 1mm, not making full contact with the wheel. You can try and take one rim apart and look how they are seated at the moment.
```

---

## \#461 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-28T22:43:17.396Z Reads: 188

```
I pulled all of my bearings out by using a printed PLA "puller".

All you need is a M8 bolt, preferably on the long side, nut, and a wide metal washer, might be not needed.

I can upload the STL if it is needed.

![58|690x388](upload://jfPcW4ovRq9c1EuxCf48t3Qspf6.jpeg) ![14|690x388](upload://7w9rDfC2oPGItoajscD5X2OnATw.jpeg) 

Best part, it did not hurt the bearings at all. Next print will be a seater/press for sure. :smiley:

Bearing stats:
3 on the verge of locking up, complete trash
3 spin harder but tolerable
2 spin perfectly
```

---

## \#464 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-29T11:02:54.620Z Reads: 196

```
Okay, press is done and was way easier than I thought. It presses way better than I thought and eliminates the gap no problem.

**Long instruction post ahead!**

This is all you need to use the "tools":
![52|690x388](upload://5oPzSMSinpslXgW65HVc1sK6cK8.jpeg) 

* Ratcheting socket wrench, M8 bolt head size (13mm socket)
* Adjustable wrench or another ratcheting socket or even a simple wrench for holding the other side (M8/13mm)
* M8 x 40mm++ bolt, 8.8 strength is enough
* M8 Nut, 8.8 strength is enough
* 23mm M8 washer (Got this from SK3 accessories) - This one is used for pressing the bearing back in.
* 25mm M8 washer (Got this from SK3 accessories) - This one is used for pressing the bearing back in, centering and support
* 28mm M8 washer (Got this from SK3 accessories) - This one is used for pulling, you can use any other of the two mentioned above, as this is unconfirmed necessary
* 3D printed puller (the big cylinder jig)
* 3D printed press (25mm "bearing")

**The 3D prints are mandatory to be printed out of PLA!!!**
PLA has the biggest strength for these kind of loads.

**Settings(reference):**

**First layer:** 70'C bed, 215'C hotend
**2nd layer and above:** 65'C bed, 210'C hotend
**Cooling fan:** 50% with auto cooling if supported
**Perimeters:** 4
**Infill:** 100% rectilinear, don't skimp, compression forces when pulling are no joke

**Files:** https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/1IuC-yWQQ25BUsvyrB41DOl68Rjvh4lne?usp=sharing
_(Small washer model is thicker.)_

**The pulling:**

1. Put the tool above the bearing
2. Push the bolt through from the bottom of the bearing
![59|690x388](upload://9p7VmMIFqrkyWmF6rzG8rrYtNSk.jpeg) 
3. Place a washer corresponding to the model you downloaded
4. Put the nut on
![52|690x388](upload://2E8hJIM00FDhWc92zcbpWgxGTh8.jpeg)
5. Hold the bolt from the top and start ratcheting from below
6. You might hear a loud pop when doing it, it's not the plastic, I was spooked too, it's the bearing unseizing(steel inside aluminum)
7. Unscrew when done and go back to step one
![36|690x388](upload://4acUWaaEJOPf8CmkMbANbdzY7Io.jpeg)

**The pressing:**

1. Put 23mm washer on the bolt
2. Put the bearing on the bolt
![12|690x388](upload://uwX0nsBcrHQEiqZiQlXLvBEgKSd.jpeg) 
3. Put the assembly at the bearing seat, make sure to pre-center it a little, but 23mm washer should take care of it while tightening
4. Put the pressing printed part on the bolt, fit it inside the slot
![44|690x388](upload://3W5gbxY47LsxpDRWbDT4aHeqO2g.jpeg) 
5. Put 25mm washer on the pressing printed part
6. Put on the nut and tighten the same way like with pulling
![02|690x388](upload://qnFyWUqmqr3hR0xX4SQmX86AdSF.jpeg) 
7. Once you cannot really tighten anymore (don't over do it, you will see the bearing seated anyways), loosen the bolt and go back to step 1
![07|690x388](upload://xS8H4QvE00pgzXhCvYiRzHfKnhh.jpeg) 

The tool also "compacts" itself quite nicely and can be kept in your pocket if you so desire:
![49|690x388](upload://n6DmP2Q0S5IWdKB8oYVCNQASmW8.jpeg) ![56|690x388](upload://pZBiZt5EfddYDWES7smDhyPkVrL.jpeg)

Hopefully this helps somebody. :slight_smile:

Fun extra: Pull and push bearings several times so that the seat becomes a little bit "acquainted" with the bearing. Makes further maintenance a breeze with pretty much no force(still impossible to push in by hand, but much easier on the torque needed). Make sure to clean the seat after every pressing/pulling to get rid off the small shavings of aluminum.
```

---
## \#465 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-29T12:58:42.964Z Reads: 190

```
Also make sure you sand/grind/file the spacers.

Original ones are 18.11mm and this makes rim sides float above each other, so tightening pushes the bearing centers out, tightening to the axles will make the situation even worse.

This is how it is before taking a bit off:
![41|690x388](upload://oIyC7sdfGFbTfNeo1aMbtiMpoZF.jpeg) 
![51|690x388](upload://oYz6DMrrOfDt6zyasfN1uKFkWD4.jpeg) 

The gap is what makes improperly installed spacer lock the bearings A LOT. Especially with load the bearings already get from the pressing into the seat.

You want to reduce the length to ~17.90mm. This will make sure the spacer still contacts the bearings, yet it doesn't apply too much load when the rim is assembled and axle is tightened.

![17|690x388](upload://6vVBrT6baS0Y2gX5PnrUuRyKLeN.jpeg) ![40|690x388](upload://limasfkjhVwvaXWpR7Ms6hiScnw.jpeg) 

No more gap and the bearings spin after assembly. Spacer works and you can spin one bearing to make other spin. :slight_smile:

EDIT: this is individual to each person. If you try to push the bearings completely to the seat, then the spacers will become 17mm even. Make sure you check your situation and take off some aluminum gradually.
```

---
## \#466 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-29T14:44:50.339Z Reads: 190

```
To finish off "Murlocs Mod" list:

Quick removal of the tyre, only works with 3D printed pulley for now.

![32|690x388](upload://8dEYwLpaGSoEjBecLiMQz3OGg7I.jpeg)

Get 3 M6x50mm screws and 3 M6 NyLock nuts.

Screw the pulley with spacer in the wheel side with the threads. Hand tighten(approx 15Nm) them so they sit flush.

![06|690x388](upload://uroeKlrK9tnfWg5F62JQefs98KQ.jpeg)

Put on the other side of the rim after the tire, put on the nuts, tighten them with a 10mm socket wrench to be flush.

That's all! In a case of a flat, you will only need to unscrew the bolt that holds the wheel in place, those 3 nuts and off goes the tyre! No need to remove the belt/pulley. :slight_smile:

![46|690x388](upload://5dcFZzrJ8srwD0EYUmFU4bImw9k.jpeg) 

That's all from me. Have fun with the wheels! :smiley:
```

## \#473 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2018-12-30T09:39:44.920Z Reads: 184

```
[quote="mishrasubhransu, post:472, topic:65559"]
There is no point in paying 5 times more for a sense of security. I just saw @mmaner post link to a set of 10 bearings that costs $9 .
[/quote]

It's not really the point of security. Bearings have different loads and tolerances. Not saying I won't try to get bearings on the cheaper side, but I think seating into aluminum will require bearings which have better load bearing and tolerances.

Even normal PU wheel bearings differ a lot. I had simple 608 bearings (8‚Ç¨ for 8) that gave up on me kind of fast, they started wobbling and locking up. Then I got 608 Zealous bearings (20‚Ç¨  for 8) with integrated spacers and never saw any more issues. :slight_smile:
```

## \#488 Posted by: captclearleft Posted at: 2019-01-10T14:30:43.535Z Reads: 173

```
@mishrasubhransu , Thanks for the quick reply.  I absolutely love these parts...  Great Job!
I looked further - It appears that these wheels are not machined the same as the ones that would fit the pulley adapter. (Although they look same, and are the 6x2's)
1. The pulley adapter lip is a greater diameter than the inner diameter of the wheel hub.
2. The bolt pattern for the hub is a few mm narrower than the adapter.
I measured my bolt pattern to be 40mm.  I measured the Pulley Adapter to be 41.57mm.

I am going to try and take your hub, and gear - fill in the bolt holes, then recreate my own bolt pattern.  Then I will have to bring in the lip about 3mm so that the wheel adapter flange is flush with the wheel.

Let me know if you have any further thoughts.  Thanks so much.
```

## \#521 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-01-23T08:10:36.538Z Reads: 160

```
For the approximate values, here's the analysis. 
I have 10S4P made of Samsung 25R battery, so 10Ah. I charge my battery to 4.1 volts. After riding 4.4 miles(~7km) my voltage reading is at 3.8 volts. i.e approximately 112Wh(based on discharge capacity plots). So that gives 16Wh/km

EDIT: but apparently that's too optimistic based on what @Maxid said. I weight  165lb(~75kg) so that along with decent roads might have tipped the scale. But likely, it's the approximate analysis.
```

---
## \#522 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-01-23T10:10:42.885Z Reads: 153

```
[quote="Maxid, post:520, topic:65559, full:true"]
It will be around 20 to 30Wh/km - so with a 12S6P of 30Q you can estimate a conservative 26km
[/quote]
```

## \#530 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-01-25T09:04:03.647Z Reads: 164

```
Here is the range update. I ran it until it came down to 3.4 volts(actually diebiems soft limit is 3.3 but due to sag it started cutting at 3.4).  And rode a total of 11 miles(17.7km). **4.1V to 3.4V is 2.1AH** so that gives a total of 10S X 4P X 3.7V X 2.1AH = **310WH**. So it comes down to 310WH/17.7km = **17.5 WH/km.**  With the board I weigh 85kg(187lbs) and ride at <20mph

FYI @murloc992

Office to work is 2.2 miles and I rode it exactly 5 times.

![image|665x409](upload://vUZoxtk6qOPuBJup7kMRtntEHGg.png)
```

---

## \#542 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-01-31T11:43:44.395Z Reads: 165

```
With Turnigy SK3 6374 and 15mm belt pulley on TorqueBoards 218mm trucks you will have barely 1-2mm left pulley-to-mount and 1mm left for the nylock nut to screw on.. I did some small mods, like thinning the spacer by 1mm and using a 12mm belt pulley (14mm) to get more tolerable nylock engagement on the axle and better spacing between pulley and the mount.
```

## \#567 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-02-10T05:59:34.404Z Reads: 155

```
With 190kv and 10s I am getting 40mph. That's plenty for me.

top_speed = 190(KV) * 41(V) * (16/50) * pi*0.15(m) /60(sec) = 18.34 m/sec = 41mph = 66kmph
```

## \#581 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-02-10T16:25:14.058Z Reads: 163

```
[quote="mishrasubhransu, post:578, topic:65559, full:true"]
I wonder what the efficiency is because of the pulleys.
[/quote]

I assume by pulleys you mean idlers.

I doubt it really will impact much(reducing range, etc) as these add minimal pressure and allow me to run loose belts.. They are equipped with bearings anyways, add just tension and minimal angle to the belt travel path.

I've found this too:

[quote="Stef, post:85, topic:30191, full:true"]
If designed properly, idler wheels can:

* Prolong belt life
* Increase torque transfer ability without skipping
* Reduce required frequency of belt tensioning
* Increase motor bearing life
* Reduce drag in belt system, increasing the efficiency and thus range of the board.

So there are lots of benefits! Of course you have to design it properly for it to work well, as with any other component on your board.

Edit: I should explain why I think idlers can improve belt life:

You can run them with way less tension, in my case without tension works perfectly. This reduces strain and thus improves belt life. Not skipping teeth also greatly prolongs life of the actual teeth on the belt (and motor pulley too if its aluminum or plastic)
[/quote]

Read a bit more in that thread, it's a nice thread.
```

---

## \#593 Posted by: Bataleon Posted at: 2019-02-12T18:03:53.999Z Reads: 154

```
I managed to fix one using an adhesive called [Pratley's Wondafix](http://www.pratleyadhesives.com/diy-adhesives/pratley-wondafix).

I partly removed the valve stem and injected some between the side of the stem and the tube which had come loose. I then put a small cable tie around it tightly and left overnight. It's been holding up well so far (30 PSI so nothing crazy).

Probably not worth the effort but finding a replacement inner tube locally was impossible.
```

---
## \#594 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-02-12T18:07:44.810Z Reads: 156

```
I am surprised you didn't get 2 spare tires with inner tube. Inner tube should outlast the tires, so even if you get one defective you are still all set. 

I had one defective stem out of 8 full tires and 8 tire-tube set. I messaged the shop with photos in Ali Express and they sent me 2 two replacement tubes for free.
```

## \#616 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-02-16T22:11:37.750Z Reads: 153

```
That's what I am saying, give it a shot and if you don't like it then change. I am on stock and I am getting 13wh/km. No point in wasting money and time if you don't really need it. 

Free rolling bearings are necessary when you are pushing not when you have it motorized. Thick grease bearings are not free rolling but are long lasting.
```

## \#617 Posted by: amazingdave Posted at: 2019-02-16T22:23:12.277Z Reads: 153

```
I changed the bearings in 2 wheels because they were clicking and nasty, the other 3 wheels I‚Äôve got are good with stock for now. I‚Äôll change them as and when they need it. 

On a side note The failure of the valve stems that a few people are seeing could be caused by the hole in the wheel being oversized. I‚Äôve noticed that there is visible rubber coming out through the hole around the stem on 2 of my wheels... it may be a symptom of running high pressures? I‚Äôm going to look at turning some thin nylon collars to go around the stems to protect them and take up the excess space. 

I‚Äôve adopted the mod to allow puncture repairs without removing the pulley... works well so far.
```

## \#640 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-02-24T21:22:36.610Z Reads: 157

```
I have a similar setup but a 60T pulley so my belts are 400mm and 420mm(to engage the idlers fully with maximum slack). You can always get a piece of string and wrap it around the gears, measure and buy the next nearest length belt (5mm increments).
```

## \#652 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-02-28T19:19:18.178Z Reads: 158

```
I always had my suspicion but today I confirmed it . 40PSI vs 70 psi is 23wh/km vs 14wh/km for the same trip(&back) of 3.5km. Craaaazy!

Give it a shot. The tubes are super small and hence a tiny bit of leakage affects it. When removing the fill valve make sure you don't let out lot of air. Even measuring it brings it down every single time I measure it. I have a lab supply that I can regulate to any PSI below 250, so I just set it to 70 and filled my tire. No measurements.
```

## \#664 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-01T07:48:34.535Z Reads: 152

```
I just rode them through a snowfall, probably 1/4-1/2" snow. The tires handles so well. Only issue, actually a major one, is that my belt broke. I guess, because of the exact same reason that @b264 had, snow accumulating on the wheel pulley and getting bigger and bigger until the belt can't take it anymore.  

Made it to 2.7km instead of my usual 3.4km. Vesc reported a consumption of 26Wh/km.

I even took a video but battery died(unexpectedly, cold I assume) and phone didn't even save the video :sob:
```

## \#665 Posted by: b264 Posted at: 2019-03-01T08:14:50.684Z Reads: 154

```
Snow breaks belts like nothing else in the world.

I'm not even worried about it being slippery.  Slippery I can deal with.

It's those belts you keep snapping... I think snow might be a good reason to graduate to gear drive

If it doesn't break a belt it will pull your motor or idler pulleys loose
```

## \#674 Posted by: Bjork3n Posted at: 2019-03-01T22:25:12.451Z Reads: 147

```
I'm having some issues with the pulley alignment. It's ok from side to side but no matter how i install it i get some movement up and down (hopping). This makes the belts go from loose to tight when i rotate the wheel. Any tips?
```

---
## \#675 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-03-02T13:23:14.243Z Reads: 149

```
Could it be a "one tooth off" scenario?

Or you can actually measure the pulley to be offset on different rim sides?

I mean, the chinese holes are not perfect, but it could be just your belt initially not meshing and skipping one tooth when turning by hand and then catching up, creating the feel of "too much tension, then too low tension". I had this exact tension variation because of teeth not meshing correctly. I tensioned motors on the mounts ever so slightly and it was gone, because meshing is now fine. :slight_smile:
```

---
## \#676 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-02T13:32:50.242Z Reads: 147

```
Ah I get it. Interesting. So the pulley is a bit eccentric or the axis os the pulley is not aligned with axis of the wheel. The latter likely. What pulley are you using? 3D printed or versa.
```

---
## \#677 Posted by: Bjork3n Posted at: 2019-03-02T22:22:35.138Z Reads: 143

```
I use 3d printed pulleys
```

---
## \#678 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-02T22:26:04.458Z Reads: 140

```
If you can spin the wheel without the belt on, you can probably notice if the pulley is wobbly or not. Or if there's a small piece of rock stuck to the pulley. That could also make it tight and loose as it rotates.
```

## \#691 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-03-05T07:37:31.962Z Reads: 142

```
In theory 9.5" sounds fine, but you'd better find out if people succeeded with these trucks.

As for pulleys, grab a 15:60 setup. It will have way more torque than 15:40 considering your kV of 230. Use a calculator to analyze the torque like:

https://calc.3dservisas.eu

I use two 168kV motors and torque should be [above 40Nm](https://calc.3dservisas.eu/?TY_BCsIwEET_JWeRbZOU6jVKT0pAsHebQwRrCz2K_-7OpIq3N8Ps7O7L3EI2e_O4T0-zUXFWYbeN8hIuylVNjIrFDAiICMUBqvKFkamLz85KcUaHBfzNzRGuI3EIxCrridxG_BUNOaxNQz4qtUK8YtyBx7A2jTy7aYFxAjsiVnopUdgIpH5hGG7qTt9nUtfjArpYthPz_gA=). :smiley:

[quote="Felixxx, post:690, topic:65559"]
Is abs good for printing pulley? Is any filament better than abs?
[/quote]

Only if you can print it warpless and know how much to scale up because of shrinkage.

I still stay with PETG.
```

## \#698 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-05T22:45:44.907Z Reads: 132

```
How did it crack? While tightening? What material?

basically the screw should go in into those holes easily, if not, just take a drill and make the hole slightly bigger. ABS is not very good in tension. If the hole is narrow, then the bolt will try to push it out. and break it.
```

## \#710 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-07T02:13:20.517Z Reads: 148

```
For the vex pulley setup, I found that i had used 10mm counterbore hole for the head of the M6 bolt, but that's the exact diameter for the head too. 3D printing might have reduced that dia even further so that when the bolt head is in there it would basically crack the plastic. I have adjusted for that and also added some extra plastic on either side of the holes. 

For the 3D printed pulleys and adapter, I increased the hole dias a bit like 6.2mm instead of 6mm for the bolts to go through better. 

All files have been updated in thingiverse.

**Does anyone have any other suggestions**?

![image|465x500](upload://zmYMawASeuu6Y4wWECWaGYNazyx.png) 
![vex_versa_assembly_4|297x500](upload://mEOnR0NVwOxSyYd1OAq1uwWc2N8.jpeg)
```

---

## \#740 Posted by: landonkun Posted at: 2019-03-12T23:47:05.266Z Reads: 144

```
I bought them from diyeboard. I know they haven't had the best reputation, but I haven't had any issues with them the couple of times that I bought things (might not buy from them again though).

They came as a set with wheels, trucks, mounts and motors for $288. Bought them last summer.

I don't see why they wouldn't fit on the OG ones. They seem interchangeable. Since the hubs with my kit already had spaces for the valve, I assume they used the standardized hub size.

I'm 6'7" and probably about 215lbs or so, so the airless tires just had too much rolling resistance for someone of my size. I'd offer to ship them to you, but I have a feeling the shipping cost wouldn't be worth it.

Have you tried talking to dickyho? He has airless tires now too. I think his ebay listing is just for the set, but if you message him, I'm sure he can sell you just the tires.
```

## \#742 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-13T00:45:38.342Z Reads: 141

```
Why would you go for airless tires after riding the real deal? The real deal is more comfortable and more efficient. @landonkun., what made you decide to go for pneumatic?
```

---
## \#743 Posted by: landonkun Posted at: 2019-03-13T00:52:55.288Z Reads: 142

```
I'm 6'7" and 215lbs, so the holes in the airless tires made them too squishy for me. It just wasn't making the ESC or battery happy.

When I first got into esk8, I thought smaller wheels = more compact, but now that I've been doing it for a couple years, I realized that bigger wheels = comfier ride (especially with the shitty roads in my city). The airless tires felt AMAZING. I flew over everything.

I didn't know much about pneumatics before, and I had seen pictures of people getting flat tires, etc., and I guess that's why I never really looked into them. But I thought about it more and figured that it can't be too common of an issue, so that's why I wanted to give them a try.
```

---
## \#744 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-13T01:22:05.039Z Reads: 141

```
Yep same, started with 83, went to 100 and then pneumatic. Never going back.
```


---
## \#760 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-16T22:14:48.629Z Reads: 142

```
It's meant to be printed with 100% infill with atleast 4 walls or so. I should actually put that on thingiverse. Along with the correct screw size needed. Any other suggestions for me?


Belt length is determined using the pulley diameter and motor-axle to wheel-axle distance. You can find calculators online. On TB reverse mount, the axle to axle distance is 100mm with lots of wiggle room. 

Please don't change the bearings, unless it has some serious issues.
```

---
## \#761 Posted by: ron Posted at: 2019-03-16T23:02:12.084Z Reads: 142

```
Yeah, I didn't pay attention about the wallcount, but its really strong. Printing at 30mm/s so the layers can be fused a little bit better together.. 

Yeah, maybe the printing config suggestions should be on thingiverse aswell. Yeah, also the information about the correct screw length would be nice. Need to measure it.

But other than that you did a great job creating these 3D models.Even the Belts which I hav laying here are fitting perfectly into the teeth/gaps of the pulley.

Which Program did you use to create the pulley and the adapter, if I may ask.?

Thanks in advance. Can not wait to get a deck for my pneu build. Too much to chose from.

Again, great work you have shared here with us. Thank you!
Greetings from Germany!
Ron
```

## \#762 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-18T07:16:42.215Z Reads: 139

```
I took some existing cad from pulley manufacturer and made a parametric design in solidworks. So now I can get a pulley with any number of tooth. If you look at tooth profile and my handle you should be able to find the post which gives you the profile. 

Hope it works out well for you.
```

## \#788 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-19T19:02:42.286Z Reads: 133

```
See if you can find the extended axle original caliber trucks in EU. That will work if you use 2X6355 motors. For 2X6374 motors you need TB218. 

You can definitely take a hacksaw the cut the hangar a little bit. Just measure the wheels from outside of one bearing to outside of the other and decide how much of the hangar you might want to remove. 

Which adapter did you print, do you have a pic? I updated the design to improve strength and bolt head clearance.
```

---
## \#789 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-19T19:06:51.353Z Reads: 133

```
@willumpie82  To me the wobble is totally coming from the motion of the trucks. Probably because you are hitting the natural frequency of your trucks at certain speed. It's absolutely not an issue.
```

## \#804 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-03-25T04:53:38.599Z Reads: 132

```
From the main post.
[quote="mishrasubhransu, post:1, topic:65559"]
What is needed(3D printed Pulley + 3D printed pulley adapter)

1. Tire with hub from aliexpress.
$69 for a set of 4 (shipping included)
[https://www.aliexpress.com/item/free-shipping-6X2-tyre-6-Inch-Scooter-Tire-Inner-Tube-Set-Electric-Scooter-Wheel-Chair/32840489792.html ](https://www.aliexpress.com/item/free-shipping-6X2-tyre-6-Inch-Scooter-Tire-Inner-Tube-Set-Electric-Scooter-Wheel-Chair/32840489792.html)
2. Three M6 Bolt, 45mm length
$7 for 25pcs
[https://www.mcmaster.com/#91292a143/=1e8wvz4 ](https://www.mcmaster.com/#91292a143/=1e8wvz4)
3. 3D printed pulley adapter
[https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/14AF8h_PFzBTdH6JRkKynJ70I3WzezC0N ](https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/14AF8h_PFzBTdH6JRkKynJ70I3WzezC0N)
4. 3D printed pulley(Any teeth count from 42 to 60)
[https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/14AF8h_PFzBTdH6JRkKynJ70I3WzezC0N ](https://drive.google.com/drive/folders/14AF8h_PFzBTdH6JRkKynJ70I3WzezC0N)
5. Trucks
$65
should have 8mm shaft with 35mm free length. TB218 will work.
products/torqueboards-218mm-trucks
[/quote]
```

## \#818 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-03-26T09:57:43.387Z Reads: 127

```
2 motor sprockets, 2 chains, chain links, 2 wheel sprockets. You still need a chain tool, which might run you up to 15‚Ç¨, but if you can get a used one it might even be free. That's pretty much all you need. I will design an adapter plate in coming days to make sprockets mountable.

Also only downside is the need to get flat plate sprockets and machine (drill press) them (center hole and attachment holes).
```

## \#825 Posted by: Benjamin899 Posted at: 2019-04-05T09:15:41.684Z Reads: 128

```
What did you mean with thin? The wall thickness or the general width of the tube
```

---
## \#826 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-04-05T09:51:45.216Z Reads: 132

```
General thickness. Seems to be 1 inch tubes, the originals are 2 inch. I have the exact same ones locally for similar price, but I remember they looked too flimsy to even look usable. The idea is, they will stretch same "wall thickness" way more than the initial 2 inch tube making the inflated tube walls thinner and more prone to becoming flat from anything sharp or instant impact.

Also unsure about the valve stem being better. Less rubber is holding it, not sure about max pressure.
```

---
## \#827 Posted by: Benjamin899 Posted at: 2019-04-05T10:58:53.153Z Reads: 131

```
Yeah Not so sure about the general thickness. They looked the same to me. And I like that stem more because my original lost air because the hole in the hub nicked the rubber on the stem. Can't happen with this one. And I like the thread at the base. Makes it possible to fix it into place and not have it loose.
```

## \#837 Posted by: ervinelin Posted at: 2019-04-08T08:47:31.953Z Reads: 125

```
There are many people who ask me for STLs, this version of the drive, that version of the remote. Of which even I am confused which is which. Top that off with having 2 young kids, having to change jobs and move all in the same month I simply don't have time to reply everyone.
```

## \#869 Posted by: willumpie82 Posted at: 2019-04-16T14:11:01.304Z Reads: 127

```
I started off with the 3d printed PETG pulleys worked fine but I noticed a big reduction in vibrations when I switched to aluminium, Also you can't tighten the bolts to far on the plastic pulley, it will strart cracking, you'll have to add locknuts on the screw ends.
```

---
## \#870 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-04-16T14:26:41.376Z Reads: 123

```
If they are printed properly, they will not crack at all. I tightened mine at 20Nm and nothing happened. Mainly has to do with dimensional accuracy, because the holes could be printed unersized and then they might crack on greater loads.
```

## \#880 Posted by: cdn Posted at: 2019-04-28T14:14:00.502Z Reads: 131

```
A little late in the game. Took somewhat a different approach. Identical deck used as mishrasubhransu. Opted to not cut the deck for wheel bite. ## \#883 Posted by: captclearleft Posted at: 2019-04-29T03:20:52.033Z Reads: 133
```

```
Hey @willumpie82 ,
I realize this is a little old, and you probably have it solved, but...  For others solving this same issue.  

 - In the video - It appears that the outer bearing is not seated.  It should be flush with the rim. 

Make sure that the bolt pattern for your rim is the same as the pulley.  I have the same rims bought from the same vendor linked on this page - But... My bolt pattern for my wheels is 40mm.  The pulley adapter from this thread printed as is - is 41.57mm.  Not the same..  If you force the bolts through, then the pulley may be off one side or the other.  
- When the wheel is spinning (in the video) the motor is wobbling back and forth.  This can be caused by the pulley not being aligned with the axle, the pulley out of round, pulley or wheel loose, incorrect seating of bearings, motor mount misalignment (not likely as the belt seems to maintain its position), and I am sure I am missing a couple.  
Hope this helps.  

When tightening the adapter, and the pulley to the wheel - It is best to have an actual **8mm rod to slide through the wheel while tightening it up**.  This helps keep everything perfectly straight.  If you willy-nilly just tighten it all up on a table or in your hand, then you may have a 1-3 mm offset within the wheel.  These are not precision wheels - They are cheap 2 piece wheels that need to be aligned properly.  If you do not have an 8mm rod - at least tighten the pulley and adapter while it is on an axle to assist in alignment.  
Just my two cents to help :slight_smile:
```

---

```
[quote="MTboard, post:889, topic:65559"]
will do a proper range test and report ba

Hey @MTboard, Great Job! Looks amazing.  Did you try the plastic, or printed pulleys?  OR, Do you notice a "deceleration" when you let off the throttle?   I am still trying to figure out why these tires have such poor range compared to my 110 Superfly's...
```

## \#891 Posted by: MTboard Posted at: 2019-05-10T17:29:51.676Z Reads: 128

```
I never tried the plastic, or printed on these 6x2 wheels. I was going to order some plastic pulleys the same day I saw Dickyho's post selling aluminum for basically the same price. They arrived in 9 days, super fast from china.

I don't have much of an issue with deceleration when letting off the throttle.  I've found that you can minimize the deceleration with two major factors:
1. Keep your air pressure to the max (70psi on these wheels) 
2. Really fine tune the belt tightness. An Idler helps with this of course. Belts being too tight really slow you down quickly. Plus it makes everything work harder than needed. Btw I am using a 15mm belt also.

You have the capability to mill aluminum? If you do make them, what pulley ratio would you go with?
```

## \#902 Posted by: captclearleft Posted at: 2019-05-14T12:15:58.510Z Reads: 124

```
@niuva, Ya I had/have that problem (debris)  with my 110 Superfly board.  It has tighter clearances as the motor is mounted under the board, and it has aluminum gears.  Pebbles still get in there...  AND - I dont ride on dirt...
As for my 6x2 board - I opted to "not" use the idler as I felt that kept everything too close to the mounts. I wasnt sure if the idler would help...  I'm starting to think it might help with "loosening up the belts".  My belts are not real tight, but maybe with the idler I could run the belts a little looser and the board would coast a little better...
```

## \#903 Posted by: captclearleft Posted at: 2019-05-14T12:31:28.553Z Reads: 120

```
@Bataleon,

Thats good to hear.  I didn't see a difference between the 60t and the 42t.  They both get the same range [(range sheet)](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1zLauFkuETBBs0kpOKL1sq-mk-qy21Do_cL4xsoutPQg/edit#gid=0).    

I thought for sure when I took off the 60s, and put on the 42's that I was going to see an increase in range...  Nope.   If anything - Like you said - The motors just get hotter.  lol...  I rode yesterday (20mi)  I carry an extra battery(ies).   It was almost exactly 10 mi when the my first battery went out...  
I now have new batteries getting ready to install.  My battery box prints are finishing up this morning.  When It's done - I will go from a 5ah 12s1p to a 16ah 12s2p...  At my calculation I was getting 2mi/1ah (at that weight).  If that holds true (disregarding increase weight). I should get 32mi...  I will update the range sheet when I ride this Saturday.
```

## \#910 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-05-18T07:31:13.998Z Reads: 120

```
I personally used two 0.5mm speed rings and one 628 bearing. Wheel->speed ring->bearing->speed ring.

If it's too much spacing you can also use one 608 bearing instead of 628.
```

## \#911 Posted by: NightOwl Posted at: 2019-05-18T18:40:11.450Z Reads: 121


---
## \#912 Posted by: murloc992 Posted at: 2019-05-18T18:42:02.935Z Reads: 120

```
Yes, a normal longboard/skateboard thin 8mm inner diameter (10mm outer) wheel washer. Most of the time they come in 1mm thickness, but there's also thinner ones at 0.5mm. :slight_smile:

![image|300x225](upload://x7zlLhQVeWgSYGPR6WlOJWMDGfg.png)
```

## \#913 Posted by: captclearleft Posted at: 2019-05-19T04:06:40.961Z Reads: 118

```
I tried out 16x50 gears today.  We did a [20 mile round trip to down town Denver Co](https://www.meetup.com/ESK8-Denver/events/261007512/).
16x50s is the best so far for me.  Great response with a better or same range as the 16x42s.  I have also tried 16x60s.  
For some reason, the 16x50s seem to roll better too.  NOTE: I run my belts a little loose.  No Idler.  A very slight press on the belt deflects a little more than a 1/4-3/8" (7-8mm).  
I am using 4 x 6cell 8ah Lipos (12s2p).  After 20 miles my battery shows 47.9% remaining.  That's pretty good.  This was all real nice flat paved trail.  

Has anyone else had such good luck with 16x50 gears?
```

## \#927 Posted by: captclearleft Posted at: 2019-05-22T14:22:50.103Z Reads: 115

```
Hey @jezza ,
 You can check out the range sheet to compare your current setup (and your weight), to see what you might expect: [Range Sheet](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1zLauFkuETBBs0kpOKL1sq-mk-qy21Do_cL4xsoutPQg/edit#gid=0)

I have tried just about all the different wheels that have been on this forum ([excluding the new TB 110's](https://www.electric-skateboard.builders/t/new-tb110-really-big-wheels/75938))

The science is simple: Bigger wheels = better/easier on your legs an ankles.  
As far as range.  You are going to have better range with your 100MBS's - by at least 50%.  As in, plan on loosing at least half your range by going with pneumatic tires.  I have gotten really good range out of my pneumatics by adding a ton of battery.  There is no way around that.  But the ride and cost is worth it.  [Check out this by Evolve.](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kGG-vy5OriI)

Another downside with pneumatics is weight.  As you start to build one of these monsters, you quickly add a ton of weight (and resistance) to the board.  

If you want a cheaper try at a balanced approach - maybe get some used 110mm SuperFlys, or check out those TB110s - Those look pretty good.  Like I said.  The larger tires are really nice to ride as in "comfort" - Just plan on emptying your wallet on batteries.
```

---

```
I just make test run with  new board. It runs very well with almost no vibration from road. I can go over grass. Exactly what I want.
```

---
## \#932 Posted by: mishrasubhransu Posted at: 2019-06-07T18:42:12.963Z Reads: 103

```
Acceleration of 80mm wheel/acceleration of 150mm wheel: (48\*150)/(60\*80)=1.5.So that's what you are noticing. 

You would also be noticing a 1.5(or around this value) times increase in top speed when using Pneumatics. 

Also Pneumatics have more rolling resistance, so you could be feeling a bit of that.
```

---
## \#933 Posted by: willumpie82 Posted at: 2019-06-07T19:31:40.100Z Reads: 105

```
I think you should get a lower KV motor, and a more capable battery, what cells are you using? i guess you'll need to put more Amps in the motors

I run 6365 170kv on 10s3p, setup for 35A per motor, the thing pulls harder and goes faster (41kph) than my friends koowheel.
```

## \#939 Posted by: willumpie82 Posted at: 2019-06-13T13:30:22.763Z Reads: 102

```
ah, i see you are using a big 40C (40C x 5Ah = 200A discharge max :sunglasses:) lipo, didn't read that correctly ;-)

You have fairly large motors 72mm, I think you can increase the current a bit more. your motor max can be higher than batt max. According to the datasheet you can load them upto **75A** con't and 86A peak at 20~50v

But other than that, I think your 230kv motors (I asume you have a dual drive) are more optimized for speed, not for torque. a lower KV motor gives normaly more torque and (i think 170~190KV is the sweetspot)

have a look at
http://calc.esk8.it
```

## \#942 Posted by: bigmisan Posted at: 2019-06-14T06:05:17.151Z Reads: 102

```
Keep battery max as it is (50A) and rise Motor max for eg 70A for start and check it, if there is any difference. But as already other told, one motor is not enough for AT wheels especially this one (is recommended for heli) you need lower kv for bigger torque (140-190kv). For this motor you need definitely another gear ratio 14/60 is not good for this motor, try 12/60. There will be less speed but a little more torque ... I use 2x motor 6374 190kv with the same gearing...
```

---
## \#943 Posted by: willumpie82 Posted at: 2019-06-15T07:27:34.273Z Reads: 103

```
like @bigmisan said, you should upgrade to dual motor (140~190kv) for this setup, AT and this gearing give so much friction that even maxing out your motor and gearing will not be enough. i guess also if you have to brake hard (if you get it setup right) you'll easilly get out of balance since one wheel is skidding.

With my setup I can lock-up both rear wheels when breaking. just brace for emergency braking and you come to a standstill in no time.

I run the following setup:
* 2x 6563 170KV
* 15/60 gearing
* 40A motor current max
* 35A current max (per esc)
* 10s3p samsung 30Q (max 3x15A discharge) 18650, DieBieMS setup to 120A cutt-off
* I'm planning upgrading to 10s4p since i get a little sag when accelerating hard (drawing 80A on 45A max battery will cause sag)
```

## \#955 Posted by: willumpie82 Posted at: 2019-08-01T07:55:24.484Z Reads: 96


## \#965 Posted by: bigmisan Posted at: 2019-08-19T07:48:57.017Z Reads: 84

```
[quote="stellaren, post:964, topic:65559"]
1.- Do you need extender axle for the wheels that have pulley or for all the 4 wheels?
[/quote]

Yes, you need extended axles. Not possible to mount this wheels on standard longboard trucks (184mm)...

[quote="stellaren, post:964, topic:65559"]
2.- I have 200 Kv 10s 5045 motors. Fine for cruising with 97mm wheels but enough power for this set up?
[/quote]

I use 192kv motors 6374, so 200kv is manageable with dual setup, but careful for gearing... I use 14/50 as my maximum... better 14/60...
```

## \#969 Posted by: itsrow Posted at: 2019-10-29T03:14:19.951Z Reads: 49

```
Haggy hubs and tyres are interchangeable with the OG 6x2 Ali setup.
```
